Let me expand the GT using the sine addition formula:
`72.331*epsilon**2 + 7.747*epsilon*(sin(T)*cos(287.774) - cos(T)*sin(287.774))`

This is: `72.331*epsilon**2 + epsilon*(A*sin(T) + B*cos(T))` for some constants A, B.

Equivalently: `72.331*epsilon**2 + epsilon*C*sin(T + D)` for some constants C, D.

Key structural features of GT:
1. A term proportional to `epsilon**2`
2. A term proportional to `epsilon*sin(T + const)`
3. No terms independent of epsilon, no higher powers, no exponentials, no T outside the sin

Let me check candidates systematically:

**Candidate 5:** `T*c0*epsilon + c1*epsilon + c2*exp(c3*epsilon)*sin(T*c4 + c5)`

If c3=0: `T*c0*epsilon + c1*epsilon + c2*sin(T*c4 + c5)` — this gives `epsilon*(c0*T + c1) + c2*sin(T*c4 + c5)`. The sin term isn't multiplied by epsilon. Doesn't match.

**Candidate 7:** `T*c0*epsilon**2 + T*c1 + c2*epsilon**3 + c3*epsilon**2 + c4*epsilon + c5 + c6*sin(T*c7*epsilon + c8)`

Setting c0=0, c1=0, c2=0, c4=0, c5=0: `c3*epsilon**2 + c6*sin(T*c7*epsilon + c8)`

The GT has `epsilon*sin(T + const)`. For the sin term, we need `T*c7*epsilon` where the argument is linear in both T and epsilon. But `sin(T*c7*epsilon)` is NOT the same as `epsilon*sin(T)` — sin of a product T*epsilon is fundamentally different from epsilon*sin(T). These are not equivalent.

**Candidate 26:** `T**2*c0 + T*c1 + T*c2*epsilon + T*c3*sin(c4*epsilon + c5) + c6*epsilon**3 + c7*epsilon**2 + c8*epsilon + c9`

Setting c0=0, c6=0: `T*c1 + T*c2*epsilon + T*c3*sin(c4*epsilon + c5) + c7*epsilon**2 + c8*epsilon + c9`

I need `epsilon*sin(T + const)` but this has `T*sin(c4*epsilon + c5)`. These are structurally different — T multiplies sin here, whereas in GT, sin contains T.

**Candidate 36:** Same structure as 26 essentially. `T*sin(c4*epsilon+c5)` not `epsilon*sin(T+const)`.

**Candidate 34:** `T*c0 + T*c1*epsilon + T*c2*sin(c3*epsilon + c4) + T*c5*epsilon**2 + c6*epsilon**3 + c7*epsilon**2 + c8*epsilon + c9`

Again T*sin(c3*epsilon+c4), not epsilon*sin(T+const).

None of the candidates seem to have the structure `epsilon*sin(T + const)`. The GT requires sin(T), but most candidates have sin involving `T*epsilon` products or sin of epsilon only, or T appearing outside sin as a polynomial factor.

Let me re-examine all candidates with sin or exp(sin) terms for any that could produce `epsilon*sin(T + const)`:

Looking at candidates with `sin(T*c*epsilon + c)` — when c_coefficient_of_epsilon = 0, this becomes `sin(c_constant)`, a pure constant, losing T dependence. When nonzero, the argument is `T*epsilon*(something)`, which is nonlinear.

No candidate has a term like `epsilon*sin(T*c + c)` where T appears linearly in sin without being multiplied by epsilon.

After careful examination, none of the candidates can reproduce the GT's structure of `epsilon*sin(T + const)`.

**GT: 72.33109*epsilon² + 7.74655*epsilon*sin(T - 287.774)**

Let me analyze the structure: it's a polynomial term in epsilon (specifically epsilon²) plus a term that's epsilon times a sinusoidal function of T.

Note: sin(T - 287.774) can be expanded as sin(T)cos(287.774) - cos(T)sin(287.774), which is a linear combination of sin(T) and cos(T). The key structural features are:
1. An epsilon² term
2. An epsilon*sin(T - c) term (i.e., epsilon times a sinusoidal function of T alone)

Let me check each candidate:

### Candidate 1: c0*epsilon³ + c1*epsilon² + c2*epsilon + c3 + c4*exp(c5*sin(T*c6*epsilon + c7))

The sin argument is T*c6*epsilon + c7, making the exponential term depend on T*epsilon. The GT needs epsilon*sin(T - c), not exp(sin(T*epsilon)). Setting c5=0 makes the exp term constant, but then we lose the sin(T) dependence entirely. We'd have just a polynomial in epsilon, missing the epsilon*sin(T) term.

**Candidate 1 verdict: [NO MATCH]**

### Candidate 2: T*c0 + c1*epsilon³ + c2*epsilon² + c3*epsilon + c4 + c5*exp(c6*sin(T*c7*epsilon + c8))

Similar issue. If c6→0, exp becomes constant, losing sin(T) dependence. The T*c0 term is linear in T but GT has no pure T term. Setting c0=0 removes it, but then no sin(T) term remains.

**Candidate 2 verdict: [NO MATCH]**

### Candidate 3: T*c0 + T*c1*epsilon^c2 + c3*log(c4*epsilon+1) + c5 + c6*exp(c7*sin(T*c8*epsilon + c9))

Same exp(sin(T*epsilon)) issue. Can't produce epsilon*sin(T).

### Candidate 4: c0 + c1*exp(c2*epsilon) + c3*exp(c4*sin(T*c5*epsilon + c6))

No epsilon² polynomial possible without exp, and exp(sin(T*epsilon)) ≠ epsilon*sin(T).

**Candidate 4 verdict: [NO MATCH]**

### Candidate 5: T*c0*epsilon + c1*epsilon + c2*exp(c3*epsilon)*sin(T*c4 + c5)

If c3≠0, we get exp(c3*epsilon)*sin(T*c4+c5), which isn't epsilon*sin(T).

The first part gives linear in T*epsilon and epsilon, but GT needs epsilon². Can't match.

exp(sin(T*epsilon)) issue again.
